  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e274d43e-d83f-4a82-8ce8-fd4880f9cc3a'
      });
    }

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer591302531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2505969260716743895">Kinda sad I finished this so quick! I really want to go on a Disney cruise. OTS optional! I haven't given this book full marks and it's the first Kingdom Keepers book I've done that with. The reason is this, Ridley has a massive backlog of Disney Charcters to use in his books and yet the whole series we've only seen about 6 of them. I just think this is such a waste and there could have been so many cool interactions between Keepers and Characters. Also where the hell are the good guys? I mean w</span>
  <span id="freeText2505969260716743895" style="display:none">Kinda sad I finished this so quick! I really want to go on a Disney cruise. OTS optional! I haven't given this book full marks and it's the first Kingdom Keepers book I've done that with. The reason is this, Ridley has a massive backlog of Disney Charcters to use in his books and yet the whole series we've only seen about 6 of them. I just think this is such a waste and there could have been so many cool interactions between Keepers and Characters. Also where the hell are the good guys? I mean we see a few of them but they don't actually do anything to help. You would think with the bad guys now organized, Mickey and his crew would get their shit together and start helping the Keepers out abit more. But besides that, this was the sort of fast adventure you would expect from a Keepers book. New character in the form of Mattie, who I liked. The kids are starting to talk about their romantic feelings for each other which was nice also. Can't belive I have to wait another year for the next one but at least we're off to Disneyland! Yay! But for our last Kingdom Keepers adventure :( I would recommend this series for anyone who is a fan of Disney. And people who miss Harry Potter. More people in the UK need to read this! And I'm really hoping for a Kingdom Keepers film! </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/444478688?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa Gabrielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa Gabrielle" href="/user/show/13410572-alyssa-gabrielle">Alyssa Gabrielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer444478688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10103900025332100613">WTH??? When did this book become so dark? I actually love that aspect, but I wasn't expecting it! I'll write a full review soon, but for now, some thoughts...<br/><br/>--Charlene and Maybeck! Charbeck! (No seriously, that's there ship name). The only couple in this series I actually care about, and their scenes together are just perfect! But RP needs to let Charlene get over Finn. It's getting annoying and adds nothing to the story<br/>--poor hyena! And the stereotypical bully might actually have a heart! Pred</span>
  <span id="freeText10103900025332100613" style="display:none">WTH??? When did this book become so dark? I actually love that aspect, but I wasn't expecting it! I'll write a full review soon, but for now, some thoughts...<br /><br />--Charlene and Maybeck! Charbeck! (No seriously, that's there ship name). The only couple in this series I actually care about, and their scenes together are just perfect! But RP needs to let Charlene get over Finn. It's getting annoying and adds nothing to the story<br />--poor hyena! And the stereotypical bully might actually have a heart! Predictable, but at least he has some depth now<br />--Dillard! I care less than I probably should, but mainly because he's not a recurring character<br />--I care about Mattie slightly more than I care about Storey Ming, but that's not saying much. I wish RP would stop adding characters and instead develop the ones he already has<br />--So for once, Jess's drawing didn't come true at all. And yet they trust her wholeheartedly. But at least it got Charlene out of being the damsel in distress AGAIN. In fact, Willa and Charlene save Philby and Maybeck! Yay!<br />--Amanda and Jess used to be main characters, where are they the past two books? I can't care about Finns love for Amanda if she's AWOL<br />--RP, Wayne being on the ship is not a cliffhanger if you already confirmed it earlier in the book<br />--So the cruise is over? Maybe?<br />--Disneyland, CA? YES. THIS.<br />--HUMAN SACRIFICES? WHAT IS THIS, Indiana JONES AND THE TEMPLE OF DOOM?<br />--I'm a bit worried about the portrayal of some of the native cultures in this book. At some point RP makes them look kind of stupid and simplistic, and while I'm sure that's unintentional, it still bugs me.<br />--When Luoski kills a hyena, it's this sudden moral conflict. Finn tries to kill Tia Dalma, possibly killed Maleficent and Chernabog, and it's no big deal? Cause they're evil or something?<br />--Did I mention this book is really dark? It is. A lot<br />--Charlene is awesome and I want to hug her and I wish she was the main character instead of Finn. Except she needs to get over Finn. Like, now.<br /><br />Well, that's all for now!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer692145112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer125338515896831978">I have been a fan of the Kingdom Keepers series by Ridley Pearson since the first book and have loved it. I'm just sad that this series is ending next year when book 7 is released in April. It's been a fun run with the keepers fighting the Disney villains known as the overtakers and getting help from the Disney heroes and heroines. They have even had to solve puzzles to find out where their friend Wayne is hiding. Placing the story on the Disney cruise line is really interesting too. Definitely </span>
  <span id="freeText125338515896831978" style="display:none">I have been a fan of the Kingdom Keepers series by Ridley Pearson since the first book and have loved it. I'm just sad that this series is ending next year when book 7 is released in April. It's been a fun run with the keepers fighting the Disney villains known as the overtakers and getting help from the Disney heroes and heroines. They have even had to solve puzzles to find out where their friend Wayne is hiding. Placing the story on the Disney cruise line is really interesting too. Definitely check the whole kingdom keepers series out if you like Disney and the Disney imagineers. the series ends next year. :( I'm going to miss reading about the Keeper's escapades when it ends. </span>

<div id="review_589305262" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/589305262" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/589305262?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer589305262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10496317910321688745">Sixth in the Kingdom Keepers urban fantasy series for kids revolving around holograms, Disney World, and a close-knit group of kids.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>We pick up where we left off in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11795449-shell-game' title='Opens Ridley Pearson's Shell Game in Goodreads' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <em>Shell Game</em>
</a>, 5, while Finn and Willa are flying through the air just after they've jumped off the <em>Disney Dream</em>. And it's a mad race to survive!<br/><br/>This is the first time Pearson has concentrated on romance for Charlene and she's torn between two boys while Amanda is frustrated with Finn who is torn between Amanda and Storey. It'</span>
  <span id="freeText10496317910321688745" style="display:none">Sixth in the Kingdom Keepers urban fantasy series for kids revolving around holograms, Disney World, and a close-knit group of kids.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />We pick up where we left off in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11795449-shell-game" title="Opens Ridley Pearson's Shell Game in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Shell Game</em>
</a>, 5, while Finn and Willa are flying through the air just after they've jumped off the <em>Disney Dream</em>. And it's a mad race to survive!<br /><br />This is the first time Pearson has concentrated on romance for Charlene and she's torn between two boys while Amanda is frustrated with Finn who is torn between Amanda and Storey. It's a mess. Then there's the hinted retirement from their DHI roles. It's not good.<br /><br />That scene between Willa and Charlene where Charlie's questioning who makes the decisions just feels too fake. As though some readers whined that the boys had all the power, so Pearson felt a need to address the issue.<br /><br />Hmm, Finn has a point about the balance of power and the part the DHIs have played in upping the stakes. And yet another hmmm when Luowski feels as though a "drain plug has been pulled". Keep an eye out for it and see if you come to same conclusion I did! Mattie has a point as well, one that she learned from Amanda and Jess, and I'm curious if it'll lead to a spin-off series or part of the KK adventures.<br /><br />Clever use of hibernation---parents might find this an interesting angle to use with the kids to encourage them to learn---ya never know what school teaches that you might need in a dangerous situation…*grin*!<br /><br />Whoa...it's kidnappings and the craziest chase scenes: under and over the water, through the AquaDuck, in caves---some are pretty disgusting, and over zip lines.<br /><br />There are some minor loose threads in this: Dillard's fate, which I'm guessing that Pearson is saving for #7; who the other kid is that Clayton found up in the pipes; and, how Finn's mom got off the ship. And I must confess that I did not like the ending. For all its drama (and the accompanying relief), it felt disappointingly short and left me with a sense of loose ends. Besides the ones I've already whined about!<br /><br />I dunno...it might be safer for the kids if they get retired…! <br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />While the threat of replacement by the new beta version of the DHI 2.0 is hanging over the kids, they still have a mission to accomplish: prevent Maleficent, the Evil Queen, and Tia Dalma from carrying out their plans for Chernabog!<br /><br />Only, Finn and Willa have jumped overboard from the <em>Disney Dream</em> to escape a pack of wild hyenas, and the ship is fast sailing away. If they don't reboard quickly, their holograms will fall into shadow, and they'll never awaken!<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br />Leadership seems to be splitting between the very intelligent <strong>Dill Philby</strong>'s increasingly superior airs, who is lying, and keeping secrets, and <strong>Finn Whitman</strong>, who is questioning his role as the Kingdom Keepers' leader. He does have a secret weapon from <strong>Triton</strong>, the King of the Sea who makes a valuable ally. The physically fit---and hot---<strong>Charlene Turner</strong>, a cheerleader at school and a starter on the gymnastics team, has a wounded shoulder---and a secret pash for Finn and Terry. <strong>Isabella "Willa" Angelo</strong> has her own not-so-secret love. <strong>Terry "Donnie" Maybeck</strong> is a fifteen-year-old artist who helps his Aunt Jelly in her shop and thinks he's God's gift to girls.<br /><br />There are three <strong>Fairlies</strong> (fairly human, but with unique powers) in this story: <strong>Amanda Lockhart</strong> is telekinetic, <strong>Jezebel "Jess"</strong> is clairvoyant, and <strong>Mattie Weaver</strong> has the power of touch. All three girls have been projected into the cruise by Wanda at the end to help. Amanda and Jess are still in fostercare with Mrs. Nash and trying to duck the government while Mattie is a friend of Amanda and Jess who's escaped a government facility in Baltimore. <strong>Dillard Cole</strong> is Finn's closest friend outside the Keepers and he keeps popping up on the cruise---also sent by <strong>Wanda Alcott</strong>, Wayne's daughter.<br /><br /><strong>Finn's mom</strong> has been Overtaken, and they can no longer trust her while <strong>Gladis Philby</strong>, Philby's mom, is their chaperone on the trip.<br /><br />Two of the six DHIs who have been created from Cast Members to augment the original Keepers have been placed onboard to help: <strong>Kenny Carlson</strong> and <strong>Bart</strong>. <br /><br /><strong>Captain Cederberg</strong> is captain of the <em>Disney Dream</em>; <strong>Robert "Uncle Bob" Heinemann</strong> is the security officer Wayne told the kids to trust—oops; <strong>Clayton Freeman</strong>, a security wizard, has seen too much to brush the kids off without thought; <strong>Rafina</strong> is a fellow security officer; and, <strong>Storey Ming </strong>is a member of the crew helping the Keepers. <strong>Andy Meyers</strong> is a film director shooting a Disney Channel 365, and <strong>Jodi Bennett</strong> is a Disney Cruise Line executive who is managing the shoot. <br /><br />Cast Members and characters of the Disney theme parks have begun to take sides. They think of <strong>Wayne Kresky</strong>, the head of the Imagineers, as the Elder. He's the one who pulled the DHIs into this troupe of fighters.<br /><br /><strong>Maleficent</strong>, the nasty witch from <em>Sleeping Beauty</em>, the <strong>Evil Queen</strong>, and <strong>Tia Dalma</strong> are working together to bring <strong>Chernabog</strong> completely to life. Somehow Maleficent has spelled other middleschoolers to do their dirty work—recognizable by their green eyes. <strong>Greg "Lousy" Luowski</strong> is one of them! And he has embraced the mayhem. Although...they're starting to ask too much. Others who have been turned include <strong>Dixon</strong>, <strong>Victor</strong>, and <strong>Joe College</strong>. <br /><br />The <strong>DHIs</strong> are Disney Host Interactives, a.k.a., Daylight Hologram Imaging, holograms which act as Park hosts for Disney. What most people don't know is that "their holograms had been engineered by Disney's Imagineers to do battle with...the <strong>Overtakers</strong>" (OTs), a dark force that includes the evil villains of Disney, eager to take over the world.<br /><br /><b>The Cover</b><br />The cover carries on from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11795449-shell-game" title="Opens Ridley Pearson's Shell Game in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Shell Game</em>
</a> when Finn and Willa jump from the Disney cruise ship to escape the hyenas with Finn diving right at us and Willa running in mid-air while Tia Dalma looms large over all.<br /><br />The title is part of life as Maleficent intones, that <em>Dark Passage</em> when "one must face one's demons", but Maleficent doesn't understand that the kids have already faced one such passage, even as they must still endure the other.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10496317910321688745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1049426814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1049426814" />
    <a title="Jessica (JT)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4754277-jessica-jt"><img alt="Jessica (JT)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605743201p2/4754277.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1049426814?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica (JT)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica (JT)" href="/user/show/4754277-jessica-jt">Jessica (JT)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4754277-jessica-jt?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4754277-jessica-jt?shelf=tv-show-or-movie-based">tv-show-or-movie-based</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4754277-jessica-jt?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1049426814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13710424352410133812"> 	The biggest problem with the Kingdom Keepers Series is that it is too long. If Ridley Pearson had kept it to three or four books, he could have done what he wanted to do with it but would not have run out of plot devices.<br/>This book dragged on and on with the same things happening over and over again from the previous books but set on a ship which somehow made it more boring than interesting.<br/>The characters never learned anything and just made me annoyed. I used to like some of the characters but</span>
  <span id="freeText13710424352410133812" style="display:none"> 	The biggest problem with the Kingdom Keepers Series is that it is too long. If Ridley Pearson had kept it to three or four books, he could have done what he wanted to do with it but would not have run out of plot devices.<br />This book dragged on and on with the same things happening over and over again from the previous books but set on a ship which somehow made it more boring than interesting.<br />The characters never learned anything and just made me annoyed. I used to like some of the characters but now they are just boring, repetitive people who insist on fighting about the stupidest things.<br />Then there are the Disney characters, which let's be honest, are the reason that most of us are here. They are nothing like the Disney characters in the movies that we know and love them from. They are flat, strange representations that show up for random, short periods of time and don't really do anything.<br />This book was the worst of the bunch in my opinion. Next to nothing happened, the kids seemed to regress rather than make progress in anything, and the Disney characters were so far off from anything that was ever shown in the classic Disney movies that I just got mad and frustrated as I read any scenes with them.<br />I have never been a huge fan of Pearson's writing, but this installment just brought all of my frustrations to a head. His actions scenes somehow manage to be boring and conversations progress in a way that no one ever talks in, especially not kids. Decisions are made in no logical progression and the entire plot is so boring and pointless at this point.<br />This series had some good parts towards the beginning, but now it is a struggle to get through a chapter without feeling frustrated.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13710424352410133812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_531236758" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/531236758" />
    <a title="Lula McCuela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16450138-lula-mccuela"><img alt="Lula McCuela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548457522p2/16450138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/531236758?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lula McCuela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lula McCuela" href="/user/show/16450138-lula-mccuela">Lula McCuela</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<div id="review_430800735" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/430800735" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1757121-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579101584p2/1757121.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/430800735?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/1757121-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1757121-sharon?shelf=disney">disney</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1757121-sharon?shelf=young-at-heart">young-at-heart</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430800735" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6301133132141391437">The sixth of Ridley Pearson's clever "Kingdom Keeper" novels starts with a splash -- literally. Two of the Disney Hologram Interactive (DHI) kids, Willa and Finn, are overboard the Disney Dream cruise ship, and in trouble. The Overtakers (OT) ... Disney villains of the worst sort ... are on-board and planning an even bigger takeover than just the Disney parks.<br/><br/>I've found these books consistently clever and entertaining. The characters, with the exception of the villains (who are who they are), ar</span>
  <span id="freeText6301133132141391437" style="display:none">The sixth of Ridley Pearson's clever "Kingdom Keeper" novels starts with a splash -- literally. Two of the Disney Hologram Interactive (DHI) kids, Willa and Finn, are overboard the Disney Dream cruise ship, and in trouble. The Overtakers (OT) ... Disney villains of the worst sort ... are on-board and planning an even bigger takeover than just the Disney parks.<br /><br />I've found these books consistently clever and entertaining. The characters, with the exception of the villains (who are who they are), are well-rounded and interesting. We see not only the teenage angst about crushes, but also the challenges that come with being the smart kid in the crowd, or the kid being raised by an aunt ... or anything else that makes a young person stand out in a less-than-positive way.<br /><br />All of that said, it is beginning to feel like Pearson is a little tired of his first group of DHI characters, as he is introducing new youths into the mix ... and those kids seem to know more than the first group about what is going on.<br /><br />It will be interesting to see how this plays out in future series titles.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6301133132141391437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_660183651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/660183651" />
    <a title="Drew Graham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3346313-drew-graham"><img alt="Drew Graham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280704207p2/3346313.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/660183651?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew Graham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew Graham" href="/user/show/3346313-drew-graham">Drew Graham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3346313-drew-graham?shelf=me">me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer660183651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2523064755861622494">Hot on the heels of Book 5's (extremely predictably resolved) cliffhanger, Finn and his fellow Kingdom Keepers/honorary Keepers/anyone who wants to become a Keeper are still hanging out on the Disney Dream cruise ship trying to figure out what the Overtakers are up to and how they can stop them. (If this sounds familiar, it's because it's the EXACT SAME plot that every KK book is about, but most especially the previous book in the series.)<br/><br/>*sigh* Where do I begin?... Seeing as how this book is al</span>
  <span id="freeText2523064755861622494" style="display:none">Hot on the heels of Book 5's (extremely predictably resolved) cliffhanger, Finn and his fellow Kingdom Keepers/honorary Keepers/anyone who wants to become a Keeper are still hanging out on the Disney Dream cruise ship trying to figure out what the Overtakers are up to and how they can stop them. (If this sounds familiar, it's because it's the EXACT SAME plot that every KK book is about, but most especially the previous book in the series.)<br /><br />*sigh* Where do I begin?... Seeing as how this book is almost a carbon copy of the previous book, I could just copy and paste my review from that one, make minor changes and be done, but that's just not how I roll. I also thought about NOT writing a review because of how annoyed I am, but that's NOT how I roll. First of all, I'm kind of baffled seeing so many reviews calling this book "AMAZING." I guess it IS amazing, but not really in the way they mean... When I started reading this time, I decided to fold the corner of the page down whenever I read something that was confusing or bad writing or a typo or didn't make sense or contradicted something the author had previously said. By the end I had FIFTY-PLUS pages marked (and that was being pretty lenient). I totally understand the occasional typo, I really do. This is not occasional, neither is it acceptable. Anyway, like I said, this book is basically the same story as Book 5 (though admittedly, blessedly, shorter), which made for a REALLY boring read. (Luckily I had to read it really fast in order to return it to the library in time. I was so glad when it was over.) I guess the major difference is that this book featured a slight twist of some kind of cop-out possible death prophecy which ended up involving a character we barely know and definitely don't care about. When I was done, The Wife asked me to summarize my thoughts is three sentences. They were these:<br /><br />1. It was more of the same.<br />2. It had an <i>almost</i> interesting climax/ending (except that it was based around a completely invented character posing as a Disney character).<br />3. I was SO glad they FINALLY made it off that infernal ship. (If anything could possibly dissuade me from my previously strong desire to take a Disney cruise...)<br /><br />So yes, the cruise line commercial continues! And this time it expands to even more thrilling excursions that tourists would love, as, evidently, do teens in constant mortal peril! (AquaDuck! Fancy theaters! Fine dining options! Zip lines and cave exploration!) So let's break this down... THE CHARACTERS: The usual dozen or so characters are here, as inconsistent and unpleasant as ever. I mean, if these kids have had to deal with life-and-death situations together for all these months and years, might they not have established SOME kind of camaraderie that doesn't include constantly snapping at each other or putting each other down?? Hormones, sure, but it IS possible for teenagers to be friends. In fact, many of them are becoming even LESS friendly with each other as time goes by, no matter how many times they save each other's skin. They really are a terrible team. Most of the time I don't even realize why they're upset with each other, most of their conversation seems pretty innocuous and flimsy, and they jump down each other's throat at the slightest provocation (if any at all). And MUST they constantly refer to Storey Ming by her full name?? I'm pretty sure she's the only Storey around. (Evidently one of the author's children is named Storey... I C wut U didd ther!) THE STORY: The story and technology still make little to no sense (it even at one point goes so far as to say that the technology is changing, but "no one understood why or how" [including the author, evidently]), and the kids still figure things out way too easily (except for the obvious things). The author is by now apparently trying to involve the world outside the handful of Keepers in the "war," but it's just not working, and leads to a bunch of unnecessary characters no one cares about or remembers. THE WRITING: There are blatant, rampant typos, even to the point of getting the speakers of a dialogue between two characters wrong. There were a few moments where I could actually picture Ridley Pearson sitting at his laptop just glowing and thinking to himself, "Ooh, this is such great writing! I used alliteration and everything!" (Even if it doesn't really make sense... "Where did the potency of possibility give way to the power of persuasion?" "...a collision of confusion" "...a chrysalis in catharsis.") There are still awkward sentence fragments throughout, and the dialogue is as unnatural as ever ("Do not say that stuff," Finn awkwardly says at one point, while later, "Amanda met eyes with him."), and reasonably intelligent children are baffled by long words like "refreshing," and think "perspective" has to do with art, regardless of its context. If you can't understand the meaning and usage of words like impale, implode, capitulate, churlish, hypothesis or primordial, I don't think you get to use them. There seemed to be several really odd and blatant barbs about race and religion/marriage (including references to "heaven, or wherever people went when they were no longer people," and Maybeck's occasional uncontrollable outrage at the mere mention of slaves, regardless of their race, and regardless of its relevance to the story or his character). The out of place pop-culture references/obvious winks still abound (Disney Podcasts! The Hunger Games! Harry Potter! Percy Jackson! [Twice!] Artemis Fowl! Even, probably most out of place of all, The Girl With the Dragon Tattoo!). There's nothing wrong with a pop-culture reference in general, but the way he uses them makes them sound like an older fellow's desperate attempts at sounding hip. Also, "bat guano" and "overtly obvious" are redundant, and dolphins are not slimy.<br /><br />Halfway through the reading of this book, I was thoroughly convinced this man has never had or interacted much with children, since his writing indicates VERY little understanding of how they think or talk or communicate. Turns out my assumption was incorrect, which makes these books and characters that much more baffling. Maybe if he tried less to sound like a teenager, especially when just narrating, it would come off more naturally. Maybe.<br /><br />I should point out that perhaps the most interesting thing about this penultimate (whew!) volume in this woefully mishandled series is that he actually tried to explain why the Disney characters the kids meet and interact with bear little to no resemblance to their expertly-created film/theme park counterparts (or he at least acknowledges that they do, which still makes no sense considering these are supposed to be real beings that stand in for the characters that represent them, making it easier for them to infiltrate the world of Disney... if they don't actually resemble the characters people are familiar with, how in the world can they stand in without being noticed?). And yet, Ariel appears (apparently without pants), and speaks in a dreamy lilt, bewildered by the idea of "tek-nology" (while also having fought this battle with the villains for decades... which also apparently started out as a fun-and-games series of pranks? That's new) and Megara shows up with some kind of mystical knowledge of alchemy, serenely referring to teenagers as "child" and being completely out of character. And, like I said, the ending came as close as these books ever have to an actually exciting finale, except that the whole set-up was based on a character completely of the author's creation, masquerading as a very well-known Disney villain. (Writing action especially doesn't seem to be his strong suit.) This general and complete inconsistency of character has always been a major problem with these books, and I'm afraid it's too late to try to explain it away now, six overlong books later. I can't help but imagine (in moments of extreme internet vanity) that my reviews and letters to the author actually made him realize something he should have realized before embarking on this project. I'm sorry Ridley, but I have to lay this all out.<br /><br />In the acknowledgments for this book, the author says, "For those Disney enthusiasts who spot mistakes, they're entirely on me." Oh, we know, Ridley. No one's blaming anyone else. This book is more of the same, and for some reason I keep reading (at least there's only one book left, and they're FINALLY off that ever-lovin' ship, so THAT particular commercial is more or less over now). As Finn says at one point, indicating the Keepers' popularity and importance to the company, and apparently echoing the sentiment of many fans in a moment of fourth-wall semi-breakage, "We're waiting for the movie." Keep waiting, Finn and Co., because to make a movie of these books would basically require a complete re-write of story and character.<br /><br />(And now I wonder if this is my longest KK review yet...)<br /><br />(... yep, pretty sure it is.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2523064755861622494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11396305899639365930" style="display:none">This is the first time that I've ever reviewed a book, but Dark Passage is definitely worth a review. Just a warning- spoilers are ahead, so if you haven't finished yet, don't read! As always, the plot raced along. I was on the edge of my seat the entire time. The characters were all developed a little more throughout the book. It was interesting how Ridley Pearson added how romance and crushes affected the relationships between the keepers. <br />And the ending. Oh, the ending. Ridley, it's official- you and I have a definite love/hate relationship. This has got to be the worst cliffhanger yet! I'm guessing that the crewman will be Wayne, but who knows? <br />In the last book, I'd like to see exactly how much Wayne has been grooming Phillby to be leader, and why on earth he wants to replace Finn. I also want to see more of Wayne. All in all, Dark Passage was a ride from the very first page. I can't wait for the seventh book to come out. Write fast, Ridley!</span>

  <span id="freeText888932493574939015" style="display:none">Ridley Pearson's terrific Kingdom Keepers series, like the Harry Potter series, has officially graduated from YA to adult. With each successive release (this is now the 6th of 7 novels) the Kingdom Keepers have gotten far more serious and the danger that much more real than when the series started.<br /><br />In DARK PASSAGE, the 5 DHI hosts and their alllies continue to battle the Over Takers for domination of all things Disney. Seeing the greatest Disney villains come to life and actually try to harm people is chilling and their greatest plan yet is to reinvigorate Chernabog whose wraath and evil will crush the Kingdom Keepers and allow for the conquest of Disney.<br /><br />A true treat for fans of Disney --- this novel goes in-depth on the Disney Dream cruise ship --- Ridley Pearson has tapped into the heart and soul of Walt Disney and his Imagineers and create another brilliant novel that will have fans counting the days until the release of the 7th and final book in the series.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2099484952206433805">I found Book VI (continuation of the cruise storyline) better than Book V, particularly because it focused solely on the cruise ship and the ports of call, with no addition of a water park or Hollywood Studios. Tia Dalma, who was on the cover of Book VI, was actually a main villain in this book unlike Ursula in the previous book. The cruise line storyline intrigued me, but it wasn’t as well executed as I had hoped. The writer utilized a few more characters in this book, particularly villains, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText2099484952206433805" style="display:none">I found Book VI (continuation of the cruise storyline) better than Book V, particularly because it focused solely on the cruise ship and the ports of call, with no addition of a water park or Hollywood Studios. Tia Dalma, who was on the cover of Book VI, was actually a main villain in this book unlike Ursula in the previous book. The cruise line storyline intrigued me, but it wasn’t as well executed as I had hoped. The writer utilized a few more characters in this book, particularly villains, but still missed the opportunity to incorporate other characters. Where are the characters that fight alongside the KKs on the cruise ship? The writer introduced character as allies to the KKs in Hollywood Studios in the previous book, but they are nowhere to be found in this one. Also, Book VI definitely was much darker than the rest of the books in the series. Mixed feelings again. On to Book VI.5.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_482703601" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482703601" />
    <a title="Merin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7319719-merin"><img alt="Merin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547322564p2/7319719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/482703601?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merin" href="/user/show/7319719-merin">Merin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7319719-merin?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer482703601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer21252211071815536"><strong>DISCLAIMER:</strong> Because this is the sixth book in the <em>Kingdom Keepers</em> series, this review does contain some references to occurrences in the previous books. Major plot points or spoilers, however, are avoided.<br/><br/>I am at a loss when it comes to my feelings about this series. It started out so incredibly strong, with awesome world-building and likable characters. I loved the inside look at the inner workings of Disney that most tourists and fans don't get to see, from the behind-the-scenes mechanics of r</span>
  <span id="freeText21252211071815536" style="display:none"><strong>DISCLAIMER:</strong> Because this is the sixth book in the <em>Kingdom Keepers</em> series, this review does contain some references to occurrences in the previous books. Major plot points or spoilers, however, are avoided.<br><br>I am at a loss when it comes to my feelings about this series. It started out so incredibly strong, with awesome world-building and likable characters. I loved the inside look at the inner workings of Disney that most tourists and fans don't get to see, from the behind-the-scenes mechanics of rides and attractions, to the glimpse inside the areas of the parks that only Cast Members are allowed inside. The idea of five teenagers being turned into holograms - and then told that their "other" job (aside from marketing) is to fight the Overtakers, or Disney villains, who are trying to gain control of the Parks and turn them decidedly darker. But as the series has gone on, instead of the awesome action scenes and battles between good and evil, the books have devolved into Relationship Drama (and yes, it deserves capital letters) between the main characters. And that's just majorly disappointing to me.<br><br>I mentioned in my review of <em>Shell Game</em> that the editing of these books has become extremely lackluster. In that book, there were lines of dialogue that didn't  match up to the speaker, misspellings galore, and gaping plot holes. I mentioned that I didn't like the fact that Mr. Pearson turned Tia Dalma into a villain, either, and considering her huge role in <em>Dark Passage</em>, my unhappiness with that move has grown exponentially. I'm sorry, but she's NOT evil. She very clearly was helpful in the <em>Pirates</em> films, and I don't like what he's done with her character at all. I can get behind the other villains - the Evil Queen from <em>Snow White</em>, and Maleficent from <em>Sleeping Beauty</em>, to name a few, because that's exactly how they were written in their original fairy tales. Their evilness, if you will, makes sense. Tia Dalma's? Not so much.<br><br>Considering that the main part of this book is supposed to be about the Kingdom Keepers' fight against the Overtakers, way too much of this book is taken up with teenage drama of various sorts. Not only do you have the typical love interest stuff - Willa likes Philby, Charlene likes Maybeck and Finn (but maybe Maybeck more?), Finn likes Amanda, but finds himself also crushing on new character Storey Ming (who is WAY too old for him and therefore should NOT be crushing back, ugh), Philby also likes Storey but probably Willa more, and, just, seriously, STOP. Chapter after chapter of this book is taken up with all this ~drama~ about who likes whom, and it's just ridiculous. I also am getting really tired of the increasing strain between Finn and Philby and who is the true "leader" of the Keepers. And while I used to like Wayne, I find him at fault for most of it, so my dislike of him has also grown in each installment. Philby is a massive jerk, who likes to prove he's the smartest and basically says things just to make Finn angry, and also revels in the fact that Wayne has told him some things he hasn't told Finn. The only character I really liked in this book was Maybeck, who at least isn't treating everyone terribly!<br><br>I also need to mention that the editing of this book was no better than <em>Shell Game</em>. It's overly long (see that paragraph above regarding all the drama) and there were typos throughout (and this was a hardback copy, not the e-book version). At one point Philby tells Willa that her idea is "brilliant" and then five lines later he tells her it's "too risky". What? Which is it? That's just one example, but there are moments of this throughout the book. Every time it happens it just really knocks the reader out of the story, which further lowers your enjoyment.<br><br><em>Dark Passage</em> is the most disappointing installment in the series thus far. Considering that the books have gotten worse as they've gone along, I have little hope that the final installment will be any better. If we could just go back to the main plot of this series - the battle against the Overtakers - and stop with all the unnecessary romantic "intrigue" then I think you'd have a decent finale. Alas, I don't hold out much hope of that happening. Will I still read book seven? Yes, because I've devoted myself to the previous six, and I want to see how everything ends. Will I enjoy it? Unfortunately, that seems extremely unlikely.<br><br>***<br><br>To see more of my reviews, please visit me @ <a href="http://ahandfulofconfetti.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Read and Reviewed</a>!<br><a href="http://ahandfulofconfetti.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380367524i/720044.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="21252211071815536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_482703601'><a id="like_count_review_482703601" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/482703601?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F15755709-dark-passage">Like</a></span>

<div id="review_588963932" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/588963932" />
    <a title="One Man Book Club" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6164071-one-man-book-club"><img alt="One Man Book Club" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516294699p2/6164071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/588963932?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="One Man Book Club" class="user" itemprop="url" name="One Man Book Club" href="/user/show/6164071-one-man-book-club">One Man Book Club</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6164071-one-man-book-club?shelf=books-i-hate">books-i-hate</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer588963932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15444472292919041589">The Kingdom Keepers tricked me! I started the series a couple of weeks ago when the sixth (and supposedly FINAL) book was published. If you've read my reviews, you know I never start a series until I can read the whole series at once....a rule I established after enduring the torture of waiting for each new Harry Potter book. So you can imagine my surprise when I arrived at the end of book 6 of The Kingdom Keepers to find there is still more story left! And not just a little! Oh, and book 7--the</span>
  <span id="freeText15444472292919041589" style="display:none">The Kingdom Keepers tricked me! I started the series a couple of weeks ago when the sixth (and supposedly FINAL) book was published. If you've read my reviews, you know I never start a series until I can read the whole series at once....a rule I established after enduring the torture of waiting for each new Harry Potter book. So you can imagine my surprise when I arrived at the end of book 6 of The Kingdom Keepers to find there is still more story left! And not just a little! Oh, and book 7--the REAL series ender--isn't going to be published until APRIL 2014! Sigh.<br /><br />Oh, well. Minor annoyance I suppose. I'll review the series up to book 6, and when book 7 comes out next year I'll just add to it. Enough. On to the review...<br /><br />I'm always on the lookout for books my kids might enjoy, and The Kingdom Keepers sounded like a lot of fun. Who wouldn't want to wake up each night somewhere in Disney World as a hologram, where you become the only force for good defending the world against the nefarious plans of all the Disney bad guys? Sounds like a good time to me. Turns out, that fun premise makes for some pretty fun adventures, and The Kingdom Keepers reads quickly and easily. The series definitely finished stronger than it started. I enjoyed the last three much more than the first three.<br /><br />I do wonder how much Disney paid the author to write these books. They are all Disney propaganda at its best (worst?). I also don't like that dads are portrayed as out of touch idiots...that's a problem in our society that deserves a much more in depth discussion. There are several instances were kids lie and keep things from their parents, and even a couple instances when the mom and the son conspire to hide things from the brain dead dad. I don't appreciate that either. However, I'm still happy to let my kids read The Kingdom Keepers. It's exactly for these types of issues I always preread my kids books, and I'll be able to talk about these issues as they come up.<br /><br />I hope your family has fun reading The Kingdom Keepers. Now I just have to wait for April 2014 to see what happens next!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15444472292919041589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_801444063" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Ashley Randolph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7393036-ashley-randolph"><img alt="Ashley Randolph" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/801444063?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Randolph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Randolph" href="/user/show/7393036-ashley-randolph">Ashley Randolph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer801444063" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17953139554321029586">Ok, this one isn't going to count towards my total b/c I didn't actually FINISH it, but I thought I should warn others about this book. It is SO bad. I only made it about 100 pages in before I gave up. I have read all the other books in the series and they have gotten progressively worse. First of, the books starts mid action. Now, while it has been a while since I finished the previous book, I don't remember it ending in a cliff hanger. Which means, action has taken place between the end of boo</span>
  <span id="freeText17953139554321029586" style="display:none">Ok, this one isn't going to count towards my total b/c I didn't actually FINISH it, but I thought I should warn others about this book. It is SO bad. I only made it about 100 pages in before I gave up. I have read all the other books in the series and they have gotten progressively worse. First of, the books starts mid action. Now, while it has been a while since I finished the previous book, I don't remember it ending in a cliff hanger. Which means, action has taken place between the end of book 5 and the beginning of book 6 that we didn't see. So, we jump in mid action and have no idea what is going on. If I am wrong and the previous book did end on a cliffhanger, I think we deserve a synopsis or something at the beginning of the new book to refresh our memories. <br />When the books started out, there were 5-6 central young people as characters and 1 main adult protagonist. Now, I have lost count of the number of characters. In fact, I can't even remember who some of them are supposed to be there are so many! <br />Let's add to that techno-babble that makes no sense, unnecessary love triangles, lack of continuity, and just plain poor writing- it all equals a book that isn't worth your time. <br />I hate that I have invested enough time to read 5 books in this series only to drop out before the final 2, but I just can't do it. Maybe if I get to a point where I have nothing else to read and I have emptied my "to read" list I can return to this one, but I doubt it.</span>

<div id="review_3446026863" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3446026863" />
    <a title="Viv" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36937061-viv"><img alt="Viv" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594300773p2/36937061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3446026863?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Viv" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Viv" href="/user/show/36937061-viv">Viv</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3446026863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6891696070396774048"><b>It's been announced that Ridley Pearson will be rewriting the Kingdom Keepers series to better reflect the Disney parks now. At the time that I'm writing this only the first three updated books have been released, those of which I read. This is a review for the first edition of Shell Game and my first time reading it.</b><br/><br/>Overall, this book was good. However when ranked up against the others, I think this may be the weakest so far, which is a shame because this is book 6 out of 7.<br/><br/><u>What I didn't like:</u><br/>O</span>
  <span id="freeText6891696070396774048" style="display:none"><b>It's been announced that Ridley Pearson will be rewriting the Kingdom Keepers series to better reflect the Disney parks now. At the time that I'm writing this only the first three updated books have been released, those of which I read. This is a review for the first edition of Shell Game and my first time reading it.</b><br /><br />Overall, this book was good. However when ranked up against the others, I think this may be the weakest so far, which is a shame because this is book 6 out of 7.<br /><br /><u>What I didn't like:</u><br />One problem that I could argue is that Pearson is not the best when it comes to writing female characters. Sometimes it's written exactly like what you'd think a male author would write a female character. I hope whenever he reaches the point where he has to rewrite Dark Passage he fixes these mistakes. (Although, in rewrites of books 1-3, there isn't any changes to make female characters less one-dimensional, especially Charlene.) <br /><br />Finn suddenly has <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[super-strength, I guess? He mentioned it's from the electrical current of the wires he destroyed in book 5, Shell Game. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> However, it's never properly addressed and just kind of came out of left field... In fact, I'd argue a few things in this series come out of left field.<br /><br />The ending... was weird... And I'll explain why. It ended with Wayne <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[telling the Keepers that the battle isn't over yet and that he needed to talk to them. That itself isn't too weird to me. But then I found out that there's a <i>3 year gap between books 6 and 7.</i> Meaning we'll never know what that conversation with Wayne was and we'll never see the end of the cruise. I had no idea that there would be such a time skip. Since I knew the last book would take place in Disneyland and that the cruise finishes in California, I thought books 5-7 would be taken place in the same chunk of time. So really, I'm just confused. I would've felt more satisfied if there was a short epilogue, extra chapter, or something of that sort that showed us the end of the cruise. Really my problem here is that I wanted to see the end of the cruise, lmao. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /> <br />This next one isn't something I necessarily disliked. It's really just an observation.<br />This book gets <i>dark</i>. Like when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maybeck gets into a coma that proves to be life-threatening. And later, Dillard dies a gruesome death. Jeez, how much more can these kids take? This would seriously mess me up if I was 16/17. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><u>What I did like:</u><br /> I liked that it began with a cold open, exactly where Shell Game ended. If I'm not mistaken this is one of the few times Pearson opens his book during the middle of action. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The whole true love's kiss where we see Willa/Philby and Charlene/Maybeck kiss is cute! It's cheesy and cliche I'll admit, but it's cute. Pearson doesn't offer us that much relationship stuff between our Keepers so even if it's small it's appreciated on my part.<br /><br />I'm glad Finn's mom is ok! In my opinion it was a great addition to the plot. Seeing his own mother under the spell of the Overtakers must've been haunting for Finn. <s>Truly messed up for his character, poor kid, but for the plot? Yes, good angst.</s> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Despite all of its flaws, I still really enjoy this series. I think the fun concept mixed in with the fact that this series came to me at a time where I was feeling really low and desperately needed a distraction. I can't help but feel connected to the Kingdom Keepers. </span>

<div id="review_2296288051" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2296288051" />
    <a title="Tiffany Spencer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52552606-tiffany-spencer"><img alt="Tiffany Spencer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519342160p2/52552606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2296288051?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiffany Spencer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiffany Spencer" href="/user/show/52552606-tiffany-spencer">Tiffany Spencer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2296288051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1411296695258202851">Dark Passage<br/>PLOT: Takes up after SHELL GAME. The Keepers are now faced with figuring out why the OT's want the journal, what the passages in the journal mean, what Jess's dream means, and how to stop the OT from bringing Chernabog to power. Then there's some other drama going on about their individual relationships, Philby and Finn's conflict over who's the leader, and concerns if they are all going to be replaced with the newer version of DHI's.<br/><br/>MY THOUGHTS<br/>*Usually it isn't hard for me to give m</span>
  <span id="freeText1411296695258202851" style="display:none">Dark Passage<br />PLOT: Takes up after SHELL GAME. The Keepers are now faced with figuring out why the OT's want the journal, what the passages in the journal mean, what Jess's dream means, and how to stop the OT from bringing Chernabog to power. Then there's some other drama going on about their individual relationships, Philby and Finn's conflict over who's the leader, and concerns if they are all going to be replaced with the newer version of DHI's.<br /><br />MY THOUGHTS<br />*Usually it isn't hard for me to give my thoughts on a book, but this one left me with almost no notes or thoughts at all. I started off this series with excitement. The concept of technology that created holograms that protected the Disney parks at night had me hooked. I loved how the adventures revolved around the parks I had fond memories of, and how well he used the villains to complement their settings. But around book #5 (SHELL GAME) it started to get less. It then it became lackluster. By book #5 I felt like the plot was dragging and I had to struggle to want to get through it. The plot of this one wasn't as hard to get through. The Keepers continue to search for clues on how to stop the Overtakers from being able to resurrect Chernabog. More battles with the villains. More drama over love triangles and relationships. I think the most reaction I got from reading it was a) when I learned the reason behind the two guys disguises and who they were supposed to be (Finn and Philby) b) Tia Dalma's trick and c) the death of Dylan. Which totally caught me off guard. I'm hoping that some things are explained in #7. Like if the bargain works with Tia Dalma to bring him back, was Finn's mom changed back, and do they all retire. As much as I'm not a fan of change I think that the Keepers are losing their magic. The ending felt somewhat "flat" and also a little confusing. I remember reading the part about Finn and Maleficent and having to read it several times and still not getting it. So did he stick his hand through her neck and down her throat? If it was meant to be a strangle that's the weirdest most bizarre strangle I've ever heard. Very unclear and puzzling. Then what was the point of throwing Mattie in and giving her this huge build up for two books, only for her to be as helpful as she could (which she does a total of about two times that I can count) and then ship her off somewhere? Then we're teased with Mickey and I'm still wondering where has he been all this time and as this series comes to an end what will be his role in all this. I'm so close to the end and I hope that #7 picks up a little.<br /><br />RATE: 4 It was darker than the other's in the series but it just felt repetitive.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1411296695258202851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2391057482" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2391057482" />
    <a title="Tom Li" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45212151-tom-li"><img alt="Tom Li" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2391057482?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom Li" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom Li" href="/user/show/45212151-tom-li">Tom Li</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45212151-tom-li?shelf=borrowed-from-library">borrowed-from-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2391057482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer497275307285299596">The sixth installment of the "Kingdom Keeper" series is sluggish and meandering. The charm that had made the previous books so captivating has diminished significantly as the series approaches its inevitable end. Although younger readers may enjoy the darker and more mature tone, older readers (more specifically, readers who have grown up with this series) may find themselves taken aback by the quality of Pearson's writing and poorly paced plot. Many of the main character arcs see little develop</span>
  <span id="freeText497275307285299596" style="display:none">The sixth installment of the "Kingdom Keeper" series is sluggish and meandering. The charm that had made the previous books so captivating has diminished significantly as the series approaches its inevitable end. Although younger readers may enjoy the darker and more mature tone, older readers (more specifically, readers who have grown up with this series) may find themselves taken aback by the quality of Pearson's writing and poorly paced plot. Many of the main character arcs see little development as the heroes move one from action setpiece to another. With the exception of Finn, the rest of the team get most of their development put toward their romantic relationships. Maleficent, although well established, remains one dimensional as she pursues her two goals: get rid of the Keepers and bring Chernabog to life. In fact, all of the villains in this story lack characterization (although this may have been intentional seeing how they're all originally from fairytales). "Dark Passage" would have been a much richer tale if we had gotten the chance to see things from the point of views of the antagonists. Instead, we get to see things play out from the point of views of some brand new side characters who were mentioned in "Shell Game" - and, no, these humans are nowhere near as fascinating as the villains in Disney's Rogues Gallery. <br /><br />I was somewhat disappointed by this installment. I think this, along with "Shell Game", cheapens the series as a whole. The joy and excitement that I had while reading books I - IV was barely present and I found myself wishing in the end for a tighter narrative with some sort of profound lesson that could be learnt by both the protagonists and the reader.</span>
  <a data-text-id="497275307285299596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2142981638" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2142981638" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6483794-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464597713p2/6483794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2142981638?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/6483794-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2142981638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6436590549470766375">This one got dark...REALLY dark. Dark Passage was definitely an apt title for this particular installment. As the Kingdom Keepers continue to keep the Overtakers at bay, additional characters and loyalties are tried. I'm also very surprised that the story took the dark line that it did...I'm anticipating some remedying of the story line coming up in the novellas and #7, but I can't really say for sure where this is going (except to Disneyland, that's a definite). These Overtakers are getting REA</span>
  <span id="freeText6436590549470766375" style="display:none">This one got dark...REALLY dark. Dark Passage was definitely an apt title for this particular installment. As the Kingdom Keepers continue to keep the Overtakers at bay, additional characters and loyalties are tried. I'm also very surprised that the story took the dark line that it did...I'm anticipating some remedying of the story line coming up in the novellas and #7, but I can't really say for sure where this is going (except to Disneyland, that's a definite). These Overtakers are getting REALLY DARK...more than just Disney cute evil villain, but truly sinister in what they are doing with these children and their plans for the Disney Parks. The detours this story has taken are very surprising for me and their travails on the path to keep the Disney Parks safe are exciting and adventurous, if not downright terrifying as a teenage child with that level of responsibility. I appreciated how this addition to the story line was continuing through two separate books, as the span of this chapter in the story needed time to develop and become fully interesting in the use of Tia Dalma, Maleficent's evil plans, and the return of Chernabog. The use of not only the ship, but also time in Panama gave ample time for the Kingdom Keepers to keep this story alive and some intense situations develop that are very unique. I'm sitting on the edge of my seat with the cliffhanger and interested to see where they take the latest developments.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6436590549470766375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/874026502" />
    <a title="Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25833304-elizabeth"><img alt="Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580497777p2/25833304.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/874026502?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth" href="/user/show/25833304-elizabeth">Elizabeth</a>
