        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25833304-elizabeth?shelf=only-slightly-garbage">only-slightly-garbage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25833304-elizabeth?shelf=power-kids">power-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25833304-elizabeth?shelf=chosen-ones">chosen-ones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25833304-elizabeth?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25833304-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25833304-elizabeth?shelf=myths-and-lore">myths-and-lore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25833304-elizabeth?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer874026502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6922693787363212538">I didn't actively try to dislike this book, and I don't entirely? I just think the book needed a lot of editing it didn't really get. There are a lot of scenes, dialogues, and words that just feel so unnecessary, and yet somehow ended up in the story. It didn't need to go on as long as it did. <br/><br/>The way teen romance was written wasn't forced (I could imagine Philby and Willa, Charlene and Maybeck, Amanda and Finn, being awkward or flirting or actively avoiding talking about their relationships), b</span>
  <span id="freeText6922693787363212538" style="display:none">I didn't actively try to dislike this book, and I don't entirely? I just think the book needed a lot of editing it didn't really get. There are a lot of scenes, dialogues, and words that just feel so unnecessary, and yet somehow ended up in the story. It didn't need to go on as long as it did. <br /><br />The way teen romance was written wasn't forced (I could imagine Philby and Willa, Charlene and Maybeck, Amanda and Finn, being awkward or flirting or actively avoiding talking about their relationships), but more randomly stuck on in the worst moments possible. It could've been done better.<br /><br />Also, I'm still slightly confused as to the motivations of the Overtakers. It's been a while since books 1-4 for me, but I don't understand why they've been fighting for so long just to control the Disney parks (or is it the world?). I also think there's kinda a lack of consistency in powers. Sometimes the villains are so strong and unbeatable for that one fight, and then BAM the power of friendship takes them out in the last chapter, and the baddies limp off to return next time.<br /><br />Just some thoughts! Middle school me would've ate everything up that happened with little thought to what I just critiqued, so I've probably just outgrown the series. I shelved it in both middle grade and YA because it has a middle grade feel for me, but, uh, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Dillard's death scene and what followed <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> definitely was a step into YA territory.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6922693787363212538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6582080-peter-and-the-sword-of-mercy"><img alt="Peter and the Sword of Mercy (Peter and the Starcatchers, #4)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1257662814l/6582080._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5bb4pwzKwXgh81zziJiYcToYKzd4Q3pwDsmX9svoh0q+YMrKWrs4BEUo+ZS9BqaVI9IUB+A1k9X0E2TMalv/UQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<span id="freeTextContainer14514116151061850008">Ridley Pearson is the author of more than fifty novels, including the <em>New York Times</em> bestseller <em>Killer Weekend</em>; the Lou Boldt crime series; and many books for young readers, including the award-winning children's novels <em>Peter and the Starcatchers</em>, <em>Peter and the Shadow Thieves</em>, and <em>Peter and the Secret of Rundoon</em>, which he cowrote with Dave Barry. Pearson lives with his wife and two daughters, divi</span>
  <span id="freeText14514116151061850008" style="display:none">Ridley Pearson is the author of more than fifty novels, including the <em>New York Times</em> bestseller <em>Killer Weekend</em>; the Lou Boldt crime series; and many books for young readers, including the award-winning children's novels <em>Peter and the Starcatchers</em>, <em>Peter and the Shadow Thieves</em>, and <em>Peter and the Secret of Rundoon</em>, which he cowrote with Dave Barry. Pearson lives with his wife and two daughters, dividing their time between Missouri and Idaho.<br /><br />Also writes Chris Klick mysteries as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/260141.Wendell_McCall" rel="nofollow noopener">Wendell McCall</a>.</span>
